Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
Ibn Karram's Anthropomorphic View
Ibn Karram's view on Allah's direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the anthropomorphic position of Ibn Karram regarding Allah's direction and bodily location.

Core Idea
Ibn Karram claimed Allah's direction is exactly like that of bodies.

This lesson introduces one of the most extreme anthropomorphic views in Islamic theology. Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram argued that Allah occupies a direction in a physical sense, even claiming direct contact with the Throne. Understanding this view is essential for appreciating why later theologians emphasized divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the key terms like 'جهة' and 'مماس'.
The passage is a single sentence but packed with doctrine.
2
Identify Ibn Karram's claims
List the specific things Ibn Karram said about Allah: being in a direction, being pointable, touching the Throne, and permissibility of movement.
These are four distinct claims.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this view reduces Allah to the attributes of physical bodies, which the Ash'ari school rejected.
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب أبو عبد الله محمد بن كرام إلى أن كونه في الجهة ككون الأجسام فيها وهو أن يكون بحيث يشار إليه أنه هاهنا أو هناك قال وهو مماس للصفحة العيا من العرش ويجوز عليه الحركة والانتقال وتبدل الجهات وعليه اليهود حتى قالوا العرش يئط من تحته أطيط الرحل الجديد تحت الركب الثقيل و قالوا: إنه يفضل على العرش من كل جهة أربعة أصابع وزاد بعض المشبهة كمضر وكهمس وأحمد الهجيمي أن المخلصين من المؤمنين يعانقونه في الدنيا والآخرة ومنهم من قال هو محاذ للعرش غير مماس له فقيل بعده عنه بمسافة متناهية وقيل : بمسافة غير متناهية . قوله : ( وقيل بمسافة غير متناهية) هذا قول الهيضمي ولا يخفى أنه ليس بمعقول أصلاً لأن المسافة حينئذ محصورة بين حاصرين فكيف يعقل عدم تناهيها .
Then Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram went to the opinion that His being in the direction is like the being of bodies in it, meaning that He is such that one can point to Him as being here or there. He said: And He touches the upper surface of the Throne, and movement, transfer, and change of directions are permissible for Him. The Jews agreed with him, so much so that they said the Throne groans beneath Him with the groaning of the new saddle under the heavy burden. And they said: He exceeds the Throne by four fingers on every side. And some of the anthropomorphists, such as Mudar, Kuhmas, and Ahmad al-Hujaymi, added that the sincere believers embrace Him in this world and the Hereafter. And among them was one who said He is opposite the Throne without touching it, and it was said that His distance from it is a finite distance, and it was said an infinite distance. His statement: (And it was said an infinite distance) – this is the saying of al-Huyaymi, and it is not hidden that it is not at all intelligible, because the distance then would be limited between two boundaries, so how can its infinitude be understood?
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage reports and then critiques various anthropomorphic views regarding Allah's direction and location. The first view attributed to Muhammad ibn Karram holds that Allah's being in a direction is exactly like the being of bodies in a direction, meaning He can be pointed to as being here or there. Ibn Karram further claimed that Allah touches the upper surface of the Throne, and that movement, transfer, and change of directions are permissible for Him. This view is also attributed to the Jews, who went so far as to say the Throne groans under Him like a new saddle under a heavy load, and that Allah exceeds the Throne by four fingers on every side. More extreme anthropomorphists like Mudar, Kuhmas, and Ahmad al-Hujaymi added that sincere believers embrace Allah in this world and the next. Another position holds that Allah is opposite the Throne without touching it, with either a finite or an infinite distance. The commentary then specifically targets the claim of infinite distance, attributed to al-Huyaymi, and dismisses it as unintelligible because a distance between two boundaries cannot be infinite—it would be bounded by the two ends of the distance, so infinity is impossible.

Key Terms
المشبهة
الجهة
العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ibn Karram's view is a legitimate theological position.
Correction: Ibn Karram's view is considered extreme anthropomorphism and is rejected by mainstream Islam.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Karram, how does Allah's being in a direction compare to bodies?
A) It is similar but not identical.
B) It is exactly like the being of bodies in a direction.
C) It is a metaphorical direction.
D) Allah does not have a direction.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Karram's anthropomorphism reduces Allah to a physical body with location, contact, and movement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah during your prayers, do you ever unintentionally picture Him as being 'up there' like a physical being? How does Ibn Karram's error—reducing Allah to a body—warn you against such mental images? Commit to purifying your conception of Allah by repeating the phrase 'laysa kamithlihi shay’' (nothing is like Him) daily.
?
Ibn Karram dared to say Allah touches the Throne and moves. Do you ever speak about Allah with bold assumptions without evidence? Read the source again: every claim must be grounded in revelation and reason. Pledge to only speak of Allah with knowledge and fear.

Jewish and Extreme Anthropomorphic Views
Jewish and extreme anthropomorphists on Allah's physicality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional anthropomorphic claims attributed to Jews and extreme Muslim anthropomorphists.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphists believed Allah's body interacts physically with the Throne and even with believers.

This lesson presents the even more extreme claims that some groups added to Ibn Karram's ideas. The Jews are reported to have said the Throne groans under Allah's weight and that Allah exceeds it by four fingers. Some extreme Muslim anthropomorphists went so far as to claim that believers embrace Allah. These views illustrate how far anthropomorphic thinking can go.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the text about the Jews and the extreme anthropomorphists.
Note the vivid imagery: groaning of the saddle, four fingers, embracing.
2
Categorize the claims
Separate the Jewish claims from the claims of Mudar, Kuhmas, and al-Hujaymi.
The Jews made two claims; the others made one claim.
3
Reflect on absurdity
Consider how these claims anthropomorphize Allah to an extreme degree, attributing physical interactions.
This shows why such views were rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب أبو عبد الله محمد بن كرام إلى أن كونه في الجهة ككون الأجسام فيها وهو أن يكون بحيث يشار إليه أنه هاهنا أو هناك قال وهو مماس للصفحة العيا من العرش ويجوز عليه الحركة والانتقال وتبدل الجهات وعليه اليهود حتى قالوا العرش يئط من تحته أطيط الرحل الجديد تحت الركب الثقيل و قالوا: إنه يفضل على العرش من كل جهة أربعة أصابع وزاد بعض المشبهة كمضر وكهمس وأحمد الهجيمي أن المخلصين من المؤمنين يعانقونه في الدنيا والآخرة ومنهم من قال هو محاذ للعرش غير مماس له فقيل بعده عنه بمسافة متناهية وقيل : بمسافة غير متناهية . قوله : ( وقيل بمسافة غير متناهية) هذا قول الهيضمي ولا يخفى أنه ليس بمعقول أصلاً لأن المسافة حينئذ محصورة بين حاصرين فكيف يعقل عدم تناهيها .

He said: And He touches the upper surface of the Throne, and movement, transfer, and change of directions are permissible for Him. The Jews agreed with him, so much so that they said the Throne groans beneath Him with the groaning of the new saddle under the heavy burden. His statement: (And it was said an infinite distance) – this is the saying of al-Huyaymi, and it is not hidden that it is not at all intelligible, because the distance then would be limited between two boundaries, so how can its infinitude be understood?

Commentary
This passage reports and then critiques various anthropomorphic views regarding Allah's direction and location. The first view attributed to Muhammad ibn Karram holds that Allah's being in a direction is exactly like the being of bodies in a direction, meaning He can be pointed to as being here or there. Ibn Karram further claimed that Allah touches the upper surface of the Throne, and that movement, transfer, and change of directions are permissible for Him. This view is also attributed to the Jews, who went so far as to say the Throne groans under Him like a new saddle under a heavy load, and that Allah exceeds the Throne by four fingers on every side. العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think these claims are merely metaphorical.
Correction: These claims were intended literally by their proponents, as literal anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
What did the Jews claim about the Throne in relation to Allah?
A) It is made of light.
B) It groans under Him.
C) It floats in space.
D) It is smaller than Allah.

Key Takeaway
Anthropomorphists attribute physical interactions like weight and embrace to Allah, which is deeply problematic for divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself forming a mental image of Allah, even subconsciously? What does this passage teach you about the danger of imagining Allah in physical terms? Take a moment to repent for any such thoughts and ask Allah to purify your belief in His transcendence.
?
When you hear extreme beliefs like those in this passage, do you feel a sense of superiority or disgust? How can you instead use this knowledge to strengthen your own tawheed and humbly seek closeness to Allah without attributing form to Him? Commit to studying the names and attributes of Allah with the correct understanding.
?
If someone today argued that Allah has a physical body based on such narratives, how would you respond? What is your responsibility to correct such misconceptions when you encounter them? Write down one concrete step you will take to protect your own aqeedah and gently advise others.

Finite vs Infinite Distance from the Throne and Its Refutation
Critique of infinite distance from the Throne

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether Allah's distance from the Throne is finite or infinite, and why the infinite distance claim is logically incoherent.

Core Idea
An infinite distance between two boundaries is a logical impossibility.

Some anthropomorphists held that Allah is opposite the Throne without touching it, but they disagreed on the distance. Some said it is finite, others infinite. Al-Jurjani refutes the infinite distance view by pointing out that a distance between two bounding points cannot be infinite. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on distance views
Read the Arabic: 'ومنهم من قال هو محاذ للعرش...' and the critique.
Note the two views and the refutation.
2
Understand the finite vs infinite distinction
Finite distance is measurable; infinite is unbounded. But here the distance is bounded by Allah and the Throne.
3
Analyze the refutation
Al-Jurjani argues that a distance confined between two ends cannot be infinite. Ask yourself why.
The key is 'محصورة بين حاصرين'.
4
Reflect on the implications
This shows the internal inconsistency of anthropomorphic views when pressed logically.
It strengthens the Ash'ari position of transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب أبو عبد الله محمد بن كرام إلى أن كونه في الجهة ككون الأجسام فيها وهو أن يكون بحيث يشار إليه أنه هاهنا أو هناك قال وهو مماس للصفحة العيا من العرش ويجوز عليه الحركة والانتقال وتبدل الجهات وعليه اليهود حتى قالوا العرش يئط من تحته أطيط الرحل الجديد تحت الركب الثقيل و قالوا: إنه يفضل على العرش من كل جهة أربعة أصابع وزاد بعض المشبهة كمضر وكهمس وأحمد الهجيمي أن المخلصين من المؤمنين يعانقونه في الدنيا والآخرة ومنهم من قال هو محاذ للعرش غير مماس له فقيل بعده عنه بمسافة متناهية وقيل : بمسافة غير متناهية . قوله : ( وقيل بمسافة غير متناهية) هذا قول الهيضمي ولا يخفى أنه ليس بمعقول أصلاً لأن المسافة حينئذ محصورة بين حاصرين فكيف يعقل عدم تناهيها .
Then Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Karram went to the opinion that His being in the direction is like the being of bodies in it, meaning that He is such that one can point to Him as being here or there. He said: And He touches the upper surface of the Throne, and movement, transfer, and change of directions are permissible for Him. His statement: (And it was said an infinite distance) – this is the saying of al-Huyaymi, and it is not hidden that it is not at all intelligible, because the distance then would be limited between two boundaries, so how can its infinitude be understood?

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think infinite distance is a valid concept here.
Correction: Infinite distance between two specific points is impossible because infinity cannot be bounded.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jurjani, why is the claim of infinite distance from the Throne unintelligible?
A) Because Allah cannot be distant.
B) Because the distance is bounded by two things.
C) Because the Throne is infinite.
D) Because distance must be finite.

Key Takeaway
The claim of infinite distance between Allah and the Throne is logically impossible because it is bounded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's location, do you unconsciously imagine a physical direction or distance? How does this passage challenge that assumption, and what specific change must you make in your understanding of Allah's transcendence?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah that seemed logical at first, only to realize later that it was contradictory? What did you do when you discovered it was illogical—did you abandon it or try to twist it?
?
The passage shows that even well-intentioned scholars can fall into logical error. When you encounter an Islamic teaching that conflicts with your reasoning, do you submit to the truth even if it requires you to change your worldview? What is one such area in your life where you need to apply this lesson?

Sects Affirming Union or Indwelling
Al-Jurjani enumerates three groups that affirm divine union or indwelling and summarizes Christian views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of sects that affirm divine union or indwelling, specifically the eight possibilities within Christian doctrine and the view of the Nasiriyya and Ishaqiyya extremists.

Core Idea
The rejection of union and indwelling is opposed by three groups; Christians alone hold eight possibilities.

This passage from al-Jurjani identifies the sects that contradict the foundational principles that God does not unite with anything nor indwell in anything. He begins with the Christians, whose doctrine is complex and chaotic, summarizing it into eight distinct positions. Then he briefly mentions two Shi'a extremist groups who speak of 'appearance'. Understanding these classifications helps clarify Islamic theological boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opposing groups
Read the opening sentence to see that there are three groups opposing the rejection of union and indwelling. The text only covers the first two in this passage.
The third group is not mentioned here; it appears later.
2
Examine the Christian positions
The text lists eight possibilities for Christian belief about Christ. Notice the structure: first six involve union/indwelling, seventh about creative power, eighth about honorary sonship.
3
Understand why each is false
The first six are false because union/indwelling is impossible. The seventh is false because only God is the effective cause. The eighth is sound in itself but not scripturally attested.
This reinforces divine transcendence.
4
Note the second group
The second group consists of the Nasiriyya and Ishaqiyya, extreme Shi'a who affirm 'appearance' (zuhur). This is related to a form of indwelling.
The passage cuts off before explaining further.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن المخالف في هذين الأصلين) يعني عدم الاتحاد وعدم الحلول ( طوائف ) ثلاث . ( الأولى النصارى ولما كان كلامهم مخبطاً ولذلك اختلف في نقله أشار إلى ما يفي بالمقصود فقال : ( وضبط مذهبهم أنهم إما أن يقولوا باتحاد ذات الله بالمسيح أو حلول ذاته فيه أو حلول صفته فيه ) كل ذلك إما ببدنه ) أي بدن عيسي ( أو بنفسه ) فهذه ستة ( وأما أن لا يقولوا بشيء من ذلك وحينئذ فأما أن يقولوا أعطاه الله قدرة على الخلق) والإيجاد ) أو لا ، ولكن خصه الله تعالى بالمعجزات وسماه ابناً تشريفاً) وإكراماً ( كما سمى إبراهيم خليلاً، فهذه ثمانية احتمالات كلها باطلة إلا الأخير فالستة الأولى باطلة لما بينا من امتناع الاتحاد والحلول ( والسابع باطل لما سنبينه ) أن لا (مؤثر) في الوجود (إِلا الله) وهذا كلام إجمالي ( وأما تفصيل مذهبهم فسنذكره في خاتمة الكتاب كان في عزيمته أن يشير هناك إلى جميع الملل والنحل إشارة خفيفة لكنه بعدم إتمام الكتاب رأي الاقتصار على بيان الفرق الإسلامية أولى خوفاً من الإملال. الطائفة ( الثانية النصيرية والإسحاقية من غلاة ( الشيعة قالوا ظهور
Know that the opponents of these two principles—meaning the rejection of union and the rejection of indwelling—are three groups. The first: the Christians. Since their doctrine is chaotic and therefore its transmission is disputed, he indicates what suffices for the purpose and says: The summary of their doctrine is that they either affirm union of God's essence with the Messiah, or indwelling of His essence in him, or indwelling of His attribute in him. All this is either in his body—meaning the body of Jesus—or in his soul. These are six. Or they affirm none of these; then they either say that God gave him power of creation and origination, or not, but God distinguished him with miracles and called him 'son' as an honor and veneration, as He called Abraham 'friend'. These are eight possibilities, all false except the last. The first six are false due to what we have shown of the impossibility of union and indwelling. The seventh is false because of what we will show that there is no efficient cause in existence except God. This is a summary. As for the detailed exposition of their doctrine, we will mention it in the conclusion of the book. He was determined to indicate there all the religious sects and groups briefly, but since he did not complete the book, he saw it more appropriate to restrict to explaining the Islamic sects for fear of causing boredom. The second group: the Nasiriyya and the Ishaqiyya among the extremists of the Shi'a, who said 'appearance' (zuhur).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a classification of sects that oppose the doctrines that God does not unite with anything and does not indwell. It lists three groups, but only the first two are mentioned here. The first group is the Christians. Their doctrine is chaotic; the text summarizes eight possible positions. The first six involve some form of union or indwelling of God's essence or attribute in Jesus, either in his body or soul. These are false because union and indwelling have been proven impossible. The seventh involves God granting Jesus power of creation, which is false because only God is the efficient cause. The eighth, that Jesus is honored as a 'son' metaphorically like Abraham is a 'friend', is sound in itself but not scripturally attested. The author then notes that the second group is the Nasiriyya and Ishaqiyya extremists who speak of 'appearance' (zuhur), but the text cuts off before further explanation.

Key Terms
اتحاد
حلول
نصارى
نصيرية
إسحاقية
ظهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Calling Jesus 'son of God' is a literal Christian doctrine that Muslims might think is valid.
Correction: The text explains that 'son' is used metaphorically as an honor, similar to 'friend' for Abraham. The literal sonship is not affirmed.

Checkpoint
How many possible Christian positions on Christ are enumerated, and which is considered sound?
A) Six positions; the first is sound.
B) Eight positions; the last (honorary son) is sound.
C) Eight positions; the seventh is sound.
D) Three positions; union is sound.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jurjani reduces Christian Christology to eight possibilities, all false except the metaphorical honorific 'son', which is not scripturally supported.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter Christians or others who hold views different from your own, do you dismiss them as 'chaotic' and confused, or do you genuinely seek to understand their perspective before engaging? How might Al-Jurjani's careful enumeration—even of views he deems false—challenge you to be more precise and respectful in your own approach?
?
Al-Jurjani restricts his discussion to Islamic sects to avoid causing boredom. Have you ever avoided studying theological disagreements because they feel tedious? What does your patience (or impatience) with such study reveal about your love for truth and your concern for the Ummah's unity?
?
The passage shows that even the 'acceptable' eighth possibility (metaphorical sonship) is not actually held by Christians. Are you content to understand others' beliefs only from your own perspective, or do you press further to learn what they actually affirm? How can you ensure your critique of others is grounded in truth rather than your own assumptions?

The Nusayri and Ishaqiyya Belief in Divine Appearance Through the Imams
Al-Jurjani explains the second sect's belief in the appearance of spiritual beings in physical forms, using examples from angels and devils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasoning used by the Nusayris and Ishaqiyya to justify the appearance of God in the Imams, and why this is considered clear misguidance.

Core Idea
A false analogy from spirits to God leads to calling Imams gods.

Al-Jurjani presents the creed of an extremist Shiite sect that used the observable appearance of devils and angels in human form to argue for the possibility of God appearing in the Imams. This lesson unpacks their analogy and the author's decisive rejection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two names: Nusayris and Ishaqiyya.
2
Examine the analogy
Identify the examples from evil (devils) and good (angels) that they use as evidence for the appearance of spiritual beings in physical forms.
The devil takes human form to teach evil; Jibril appeared as Dihya or a bedouin.
3
See the conclusion
Understand how they apply this analogy to God appearing in the pure progeny (the Imams). They claim it is not impossible for God to manifest in perfect humans, especially the Imams.
They go so far as to call the Imams 'gods'.
4
Note the refutation
Observe that the author calls this 'clear misguidance' without further elaboration, implying the analogy is invalid and the belief is false.
The brevity of the refutation shows the author's certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الثانية النصيرية والإسحاقية من غلاة الشيعة قالوا ظهور الروحاني بالجسماني لا ينكر ففي طرف الشر كالشياطين فإنه كثيراً ما يتصور الشيطان بصورة إنسان ليعلمه الشر ويكلمه بلسانه وفي طرف الخير كالملائكة فإن جبريل كان يظهر بصورة دحية الكلبي والأعرابي فلا يمتنع حينئذ أن يظهره الله تعالى في صورة بعض الكاملين وأولى الخلق بذلك أشرفهم وأكملهم وهو العترة الطاهرة وهو من يظهر فيه العلم التام والقدرة التامة من الأئمة من تلك العترة ولم يتحاشوا عن إطلاق الآلهة على أئمتهم وهذه ضلالة بينة
The second sect: the Nusayris and the Ishaqiyya from the extremists of the Shi'a said: The appearance of the spiritual in the physical is not denied. For in the realm of evil, like the devils, it often happens that the devil takes the form of a human to teach him evil and speak with his tongue. And in the realm of good, like the angels, Jibril used to appear in the form of Dihya al-Kalbi and a bedouin. So it is not impossible, then, that God should manifest Himself in the form of some perfect ones, and the most worthy of creation for that are the most noble and perfect, namely the pure progeny (al-'itra al-tāhira), and it is in them that complete knowledge and complete power appear from the Imams of that progeny. And they did not shy away from applying the term 'gods' to their Imams, and this is clear misguidance.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents the creed of the Nusayris and Ishaqiyya, extremist Shiite groups. They argue from the fact that spiritual beings like devils and angels can appear in physical forms—devils as humans to teach evil, angels as companions to deliver revelation—that it is possible for God to appear in a physical form as well. They claim that the most suitable forms are the perfect humans, specifically the pure progeny (the Imams from the household of the Prophet). They went so far as to call their Imams 'gods', which the author labels as clear misguidance. Note that the author does not accept their analogy; he simply reports and refutes it implicitly by calling it misguidance.

Key Terms
الروحاني
الجسماني
العترة
الأئمة
الآلهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The appearance of spiritual beings in physical forms proves that God can also appear in a physical form.
Correction: The author rejects this reasoning as clear misguidance, because God's transcendence is absolute and cannot be compared to created spirits.

Checkpoint
Why do the Nusayris believe God can appear in the form of the Imams?
A) Because spiritual beings appear physically
B) Because the Imams are gods
C) Because the Qur'an says so
D) Because of miracles

Key Takeaway
The Nusayris and Ishaqiyya erroneously analogized from the appearance of spirits to justify calling their Imams gods, which is clearly misguided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Commit to one action this week to ensure your allegiance remains to Allah alone.
?
The Nusayris were sincere in their devotion to their Imams, but they were led astray by a false analogy. Reflect on your own devotions: are there any practices or beliefs you hold that you have never critically examined against the Qur'an and Sunnah? How can you test them this month to ensure you are not following a similar path of misguidance?
?
This passage calls the belief in divine appearance through the Imams 'clear misguidance.' Yet, misguidance often feels convincing. When have you been convinced by an argument that seemed logical but later realized it conflicted with core Islamic principles? How can you strengthen your ability to detect false analogies in matters of 'aqeedah? Write one concrete step you will take.

The Error of the Existential Sufis: Denying Otherness
Al-Jurjani critiques a Sufi subgroup that denies otherness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the existential Sufi claim that 'only God exists' is considered even more erroneous than the Christian doctrines of indwelling and union.

Core Idea
Denying otherness leads to an absurd mixing of Creator and creation.

This passage presents a third sect: some Sufis whose views are jumbled between doctrines of union and indwelling. Among them, a subgroup known as the 'existential Sufis' goes further, rejecting both concepts because they imply otherness. They assert that nothing exists but God—a pantheistic monism. Al-Jurjani refutes this view as even more corrupt than the earlier ones, as it entails an irrational mixing of the divine with the created. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the author's tone: he describes the third group as confused and summarizes their position by reference to the Christians.
2
Identify the two positions mentioned
The passage contains two distinct views: 1) Some Sufis confuse ḥulūl (indwelling) and ittiḥād (union) like Christians. 2) The existential Sufis deny both because they reject otherness. Distinguish these.
The existential Sufis are a subset within the third sect.
3
Understand the existential Sufi argument
They say: 'No indwelling, no union—because these imply otherness. We don't affirm otherness. Rather, in the abode of existence there is none other than He.' This is a monistic claim: only God exists.
4
Grasp the author's refutation
Al-Jurjani says this excuse is 'more severe in ugliness and falsehood' than the earlier assertion. Why? Because it necessarily leads to 'mixing' (mukhālaṭa)—an inextricable blending of Creator and creation—which no rational person would accept.
The core problem: if only God exists, then the distinction between God and the world collapses, leading to absurd consequences.
5
Reflect on the key takeaway
The lesson shows that preserving tawḥīd does not mean denying all distinction. Proper transcendence (tanzīh) requires affirming that God is not mixed with creation. The existential Sufi position is a distortion of tawḥīd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الثالثة : بعض المتصوفة وكلامهم مخبط بين الحلول والاتحاد والضبط ما ذكرناه في قول النصارى والكل باطل سوى أنه تعالى خص أولياءه بخوارق عادات كرامة لهم ورأيت من الصوفية الوجودية من ينكره ويقول لا حلول ولا اتحاد إذ كل ذلك يشعر بالغيرية ونحن لا نقول بها بل نقول ليس في دار الوجود غيره ديار وهذا العذر أشد قبحاً وبطلاناً من ذلك الجزم إذ يلزم تلك المخالطة التي لا يجترئ على القول بها عاقل ولا مميز أدنى تمييز
The third sect: some of the Sufis. Their speech is confused between indwelling (ḥulūl) and union (ittiḥād). The summary is what we mentioned in the statement of the Christians. And all of it is false, except that He, exalted, distinguishes His saints with miraculous occurrences as a kindness to them. And I have seen among the existential Sufis (al-ṣūfiyya al-wujūdiyya) some who deny that and say: 'There is no indwelling and no union, because all of that implies otherness, and we do not affirm otherness. Rather, we say: In the abode of existence there is none other than He.' And this excuse is more severe in ugliness and falsehood than that categorical assertion, because it necessarily entails that mixing (mukhālaṭa) which no intelligent person, even with the least discernment, would dare to say.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage addresses the third group: some Sufis. Their views are confused between indwelling and union. The author states that the summary of their position is the same as that of the Christians (i.e., they fall into the same errors). However, there is a subset called the 'existential Sufis' (al-ṣūfiyya al-wujūdiyya) who deny both indwelling and union. They argue that such concepts imply duality or otherness, and they claim that there is no existence besides God. This is a form of pantheistic monism. The author dismisses this as even worse than the previous positions because it leads to a mixing of the divine and created that no rational person would accept.

Key Terms
الحلول
الاتحاد
الصوفية الوجودية
الغيرية
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that denying otherness and affirming that only God exists is a form of pure tawḥīd.
Correction: Al-Jurjani shows that this leads to an unacceptable mixing (mukhālaṭa) of Creator and creation, which is even more false than affirming indwelling or union.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author consider the view of the existential Sufis worse than that of the Christians?
A) Because they deny indwelling and union but claim there is no other existence, leading to a confusion that defies reason.
B) Because they are more extreme in their worship of the Imams.
C) Because they reject miracles.
D) Because they are polytheists.

Key Takeaway
Preserving divine transcendence requires affirming a real distinction between Creator and creation; the existential Sufi denial of otherness collapses this distinction and is rationally untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself treating people, possessions, or circumstances as if they were ultimate—blurring the line between Creator and creation? How can this lesson sharpen your vigilance against even subtle shirk?
?
The existential Sufi claim 'there is none other than He' sounds beautiful and spiritual. Yet the author calls it absurd. Is there a belief you hold that feels profound but, when scrutinized by reason, actually confuses the role of the Creator? Will you commit to testing your cherished ideas against clear theological reasoning?
?
When you say 'God is with me,' do you ever imagine a physical closeness that compromises His transcendence? How does this lesson's insistence on otherness deepen your understanding of God's nearness without mixing?

Sectarian Positions on Temporal Events in God
Enumeration of three sectarian positions on hawadith in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main sectarian positions—majority, Magians, and Karramiyya—on whether temporal events can subsist in God.

Core Idea
Three groups debate whether God can be a locus for temporal events.

Islamic theology has debated whether temporal events (hawadith) can occur in God's essence. This passage presents the views of the majority, the Magians, and the Karramiyya, each with a different position on the matter. Understanding these positions is foundational for later discussions on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the three positions.
2
Identify the three sects
Find the three groups mentioned: the majority (Jumhur), the Magians, and the Karramiyya.
Notice how each group's view is defined.
3
Compare their views
Contrast the positions: the majority denies temporal events in God, the Magians allow all perfection attributes, and the Karramiyya allow only those needed for creation.
The Karramiyya condition is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد اختلف في كونه تعالى محل الحوادث فمنعه الجمهور من أرباب الملل وغيرهم وقال المجوس كل حادث هو من صفات الكمال قائم به وقال الكرامية يجوز قيام الحادث به لا مطلقاً بل كل حادث يحتاج الباري تعالى إليه في الإيجاد ثم اختلفوا في ذلك الحادث فقيل هو الإرادة وقيل هو قوله كن واتفقوا على أنه يسمى حادثا وما لا يقوم بذاته من الحوادث يسمى محدثا فرقا بينهما
So there is disagreement concerning His being a locus for temporal events. The majority among the adherents of religions and others prevented it. The Magians said: Every temporal event that is an attribute of perfection subsists in Him. The Karramiyya said: It is permissible for a temporal event to subsist in Him, not absolutely, but every temporal event that the Exalted Creator needs for creation. Then they differed concerning that temporal event: it was said it is the will, and it was said it is His word 'Be'. And they agreed that it is called 'temporal event' (hadith), and what does not subsist in His essence from among the temporal events is called 'created thing' (muhdath), as a distinction between them.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a classification of sectarian positions on whether temporal events (hawadith) can subsist in God's essence. It begins by stating that there is disagreement on the matter. Three groups are mentioned: (1) The majority (al-Jumhur), including Muslims and others, absolutely deny that God can be a locus for temporal events. (2) The Magians (al-Majus) assert that every temporal event that is a perfection attribute, such as creation itself, subsists in God. (3) The Karramiyya hold a middle position: temporal events can subsist in God, but only those that God needs for creating—specifically, they debated whether this is the divine will (al-irada) or the creative command 'Be' (kun). Despite their differences, all groups agree on a terminological distinction: a temporal event that subsists in God's essence is called 'hadith' (event), while a temporal event that does not subsist in God (i.e., created entities) is called 'muhdath' (created thing). This distinction emphasizes that the term 'hadith' is reserved for events directly qualifying the divine essence.

Key Terms
الجمهور
المجوس
الكرامية
الحادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyya allowed all temporal events in God.
Correction: The Karramiyya restricted it to temporal events that God needs for creation, not any event.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group holds that temporal events can subsist in God only if He needs them for creation?
A) The majority (Jumhur)
B) The Magians
C) The Karramiyya
D) All three groups

Key Takeaway
The three sectarian positions—denial, full allowance, and conditional allowance—define the spectrum of views on temporal events in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's ability to create and act, do you ever unconsciously restrict Him to your own categories of 'perfection'? What does this passage reveal about how far human reasoning can go in defining God?
?
The Magians attributed every temporal event of perfection to God. Are there any 'temporal' aspects of your life (your daily actions, thoughts, or creations) that you take pride in as if they were independent of God's sustenance? How does this passage remind you of the complete dependence of all things on God?
?
The Karramiyya conditionally allowed only what God needs for creation. Do you approach your understanding of God's actions with the humility to accept that His wisdom might require things beyond your comprehension? What would it mean for you to trust in God's 'needs'—given that He has no needs—except the need to manifest His mercy and justice?

Distinguishing Hadith and Muhdath
Distinction between hadith and muhdath with internal Karramiyya disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the terminological distinction between hadith (temporal event in God) and muhdath (created thing), and the internal Karramiyya debate over whether that temporal event is the will or the command 'Be'.

Core Idea
A temporal event in God is called hadith; a created thing is called muhdath.

After presenting the sectarian views, the passage delves into a technical distinction: between a temporal event that subsists in God (hadith) and a temporal event that does not (muhdath). This distinction is crucial for understanding later theological discussions on God's attributes and the nature of divine acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation about the internal debate and terminology.
2
Identify the two opinions
The Karramiyya differed: was the temporal event the will or the command 'Be'?
Both are acts of creation.
3
Understand the distinction
They agreed that a temporal event subsisting in God is called 'hadith', while one not subsisting is 'muhdath'.
This distinction clarifies terminology.

Source Text

Checkpoint

B) The temporal event in God is called hadith

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Karramiyya were so careful about language regarding God that they invented a technical distinction. When you speak about God—in prayer, conversation, or even your thoughts—do you guard your words with similar precision, or do you sometimes speak loosely, reducing His majesty? What specific phrase will you correct starting today?
?

?
The Karramiyya agreed on a distinction that separates God's internal actions from created things. In your daily life, do you blur the line between what belongs to God and what is mere creation? When you attribute success, failure, or changes to God, do you truly recognize His transcendence, or do you treat Him as just another cause within the world? Commit to one way you will honor this distinction in your thoughts today.

Dualists vs. Polytheists: The Manichaeans
Al-Jurjani distinguishes dualists from polytheists and describes Manichaean beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological distinction between polytheists (mushrikun) and dualists (al-thunawiyya), and the beliefs of the Manichaean sect regarding good and evil.

Core Idea
Dualists claim two eternal principles, while polytheists do not.

Al-Jurjani clarifies that only dualists affirm two necessary existents; polytheists merely worship multiple beings without attributing divinity to them. He then discusses the Manichaeans as an example of dualist belief, noting their acceptance of prophets and moral code.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mushrikun from dualists
Read the opening lines where al-Jurjani explains that polytheists are not considered to believe in two necessary existents. Understand the difference.
Polytheists are those who worship multiple beings, but dualists are those who posit two eternal creators.
2
Identify the dualist sects mentioned
The passage names the Manichaeans, Daysanites, and Mazdakites as dualist sects. Note that the text focuses on the Manichaeans.
3
Examine Manichaean beliefs
The passage provides details about Manichaean beliefs: their founder Mani, their acceptance of a series of prophets, and their moral practices (four daily prayers, prohibitions).
The text is incomplete, so we only have a partial picture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا يقولون بإلهين واجبي الوجود إلخ) فعدهم من المشركين لقولهم بتعدد المستحق للعبادة لا لقولهم بواجبي الوجود. قوله: (فالمانوية والديصانية من الثنوية قالوا إلخ) لا فائدة في التخصيص فإن المزدكية أيضاً قالوا بذلك، أما المانوية فهو أصحاب ماني بن ماني الحكيم الذي ظهر في زمان شابور بن از دشير وقتله بهرام بن هرمز بن شابور بعدما بعث عيسى عليه السلام وهم معتقدون في الشرائع والأنبياء وأن أول مبعوث بالحكمة والنبوة آدم عليه السلام ثم شيث ونوح وإبراهيم وزرداشت والمسيح ويونس ومحمد صلوات الله عليه وعلى سائر انبيائه وكانوا يوجبون في اليوم والليلة أربع صلوات ويحرمون الزنا والقتل والسرقة والكذب والسحر وعبادة الأوثان وغير ذلك، وأما
His statement: (They do not say that there are two necessary existents, etc.) So he counts them among the polytheists because they say there are multiple beings worthy of worship, not because they say there are two necessary existents. His statement: (The Manichaeans and Daysanites from among the dualists said, etc.) There is no benefit in specification, for the Mazdakites also said that. As for the Manichaeans, they are the followers of Mani ibn Mani the philosopher who appeared in the time of Shapur ibn Ardashir and was killed by Bahram ibn Hurmuz ibn Shapur after the mission of Jesus, peace be upon him. They believe in the laws and prophets, and that the first sent with wisdom and prophethood was Adam, peace be upon him, then Seth, Noah, Abraham, Zoroaster, the Messiah, Jonah, and Muhammad—peace of God be upon him and upon all his prophets. They required four prayers daily and forbade adultery, murder, theft, lying, sorcery, idol worship, and so on. And as for...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the only group that truly believes in two necessary existents (wājibay al-wujūd) are the dualists (al-thunawiyya). The polytheists (mushrikūn) who worship idols are not considered to believe in two necessary gods; they use idols as intermediaries. Among the dualists, the Manichaeans and Daysanites are mentioned, but the commentary notes that the Mazdakites also hold similar views. The text then provides some details about Manichaeans: they follow Mani, a philosopher in the Sassanian period; they believe in a series of prophets including Adam, Seth, Noah, Abraham, Zoroaster, Jesus, Jonah, and Muhammad; and they practice four daily prayers and forbid various sins. The passage is incomplete, breaking off at 'and as for'.

مانوية
ديصانية
مزدكية
مشركون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that polytheists who worship multiple gods believe in multiple necessary existents.
Correction: The text clarifies that polytheists do not attribute divinity to idols; only dualists claim two eternal principles.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the dualists (al-thunawiyya) believe in two creators?
A) Because they observed that good and evil arise from the same source.
B) Because they thought the one god cannot be both good and evil, so each requires a separate agent.
C) Because they rejected all prophecies.
D) Because they believed in reincarnation.

Key Takeaway
Dualists, unlike polytheists, posit two eternal principles (good and evil) and include sects like Manichaeans who accept prophets and practice rituals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Manichaeans believed in many prophets and performed daily prayers, yet they were still dualists. Are there any beliefs or practices in your own life that seem 'Islamic' on the surface but are rooted in a dualistic or compromised worldview? What would it take to align your heart entirely with tawhid?
?
Al-Jurjani carefully distinguished between polytheists and dualists. Does your understanding of shirk stop at external actions, or do you examine the principles behind your worship? How can you ensure that you are not inadvertently attributing ultimate power to something other than Allah?
?
The passage shows that even those who accept many prophets can be misguided in their theology. How does this challenge you to prioritize sound belief over mere ritual? Will you take time this week to learn more about the foundations of aqeedah to protect yourself from error?

Why Dualists Are Considered Polytheists
Al-Jurjani clarifies the criterion for considering dualists as polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Jurjani classifies dualists as polytheists based on their affirmation of multiple objects of worship rather than two necessary existents.

Core Idea
Dualists are polytheists because they worship multiple beings, not because they claim two gods.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction: dualists are considered polytheists (mushrikūn) because they hold multiple objects worthy of worship, not merely because they assert two necessary existents. Al-Jurjani also corrects the original text for not including the Mazdakites among those who hold this view.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Notice how al-Jurjani explains why dualists are counted as polytheists. Pay attention to the negation 'لا يقولون بإلهين واجبي الوجود' which sets up the refutation.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Identify the two possible reasons for considering them polytheists: claiming two gods vs. claiming multiple objects of worship. The author specifies it is the latter.
The phrase 'لا لقولهم بواجبي الوجود' is crucial.
3
Understand the corrective remark
The author points out that the original text's specification of Manichaeans and Daysanites is incomplete; the Mazdakites also share this belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا يقولون بإلهين واجبي الوجود إلخ) فعدهم من المشركين لقولهم بتعدد المستحق للعبادة لا لقولهم بواجبي الوجود. قوله: (فالمانوية والديصانية من الثنوية قالوا إلخ) لا فائدة في التخصيص فإن المزدكية أيضاً قالوا بذلك، أما المانوية فهو أصحاب ماني بن ماني الحكيم الذي ظهر في زمان شابور بن از دشير وقتله بهرام بن هرمز بن شابور بعدما بعث عيسى عليه السلام وهم معتقدون في الشرائع والأنبياء وأن أول مبعوث بالحكمة والنبوة آدم عليه السلام ثم شيث ونوح وإبراهيم وزرداشت والمسيح ويونس ومحمد صلوات الله عليه وعلى سائر انبيائه وكانوا يوجبون في اليوم والليلة أربع صلوات ويحرمون الزنا والقتل والسرقة والكذب والسحر وعبادة الأوثان وغير ذلك، وأما الظلمة، وفساده ظاهر لأنهما عرضان فيلزم قدم الجسم وكون الإله محتاجاً إليه وكأنهم أرادوا معنى آخر سوى المتعارف فإنهم قالوا النورحي عالم قادر سميع بصير، والمجوس منهم ذهبوا إلى أن فاعل الخير هو يزدان وفاعل الشر هو اهر من ويعنون به الشيطان، قوله : ( وفاعل الشر هواهر من إلخ) واختلف المجوس في أن أهو من قديم أو حادث من يزدان.
His statement: (They do not affirm two necessary existent gods, etc.) So he counts them among the polytheists because of their claim of multiple objects worthy of worship, not because of their claim of two necessary existents. His statement: (The Manichaeans and the Daysānites among the dualists said, etc.) There is no benefit in specification, for the Mazdakites also said that. As for the Manichaeans, they are the followers of Mani son of Mani the sage, who appeared in the time of Shapur son of Ardashir, and was killed by Bahram son of Hormuz son of Shapur after the mission of Jesus, peace be upon him. They believe in the laws and prophets, and that the first sent with wisdom and prophecy was Adam, peace be upon him, then Seth, Noah, Abraham, Zoroaster, the Messiah, Jonah, and Muhammad, may God's blessings be upon him and all his prophets. They required four prayers each day and night, and forbade adultery, murder, theft, lying, sorcery, idol worship, and other things. As for darkness, its corruption is apparent because they are accidents, necessitating the pre-eternity of the body and the god's need of it. It is as if they intended another meaning besides the conventional one, for they said the Light is living, knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing. Among them, the Magians held that the doer of good is Yazdān and the doer of evil is Ahriman, meaning Satan. His statement: (And the doer of evil is Ahriman, etc.) The Magians differed as to whether Ahriman is pre-eternal or originated from Yazdān.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a classification of dualist sects (thunawiyya) and a clarification of why they are considered polytheists. The author first explains that dualists are called polytheists (mushrikūn) because they affirm multiple objects worthy of worship, not because they affirm two necessary existents. He then criticizes the original text for specifying only Manichaeans and Daysānites, noting that the Mazdakites also hold the same view. A detailed description of the Manichaeans follows: their founder Mani, his time, and his death. They believe in prophets and perform four daily prayers, forbidding various sins. The description then turns to their view of darkness as corrupt, leading to logical problems such as the pre-eternity of bodies and God's need of them. The author suggests they may have meant something other than the conventional meaning, as they attribute life, knowledge, power, hearing, and sight to Light. Then he mentions the Magians: they distinguish Yazdān as the doer of good and Ahriman (Satan) as the doer of evil. There is a disagreement among the Magians about whether Ahriman is pre-eternal or originated from Yazdān.

Key Terms
ثنوية
مشركون
مزدكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The misconception that dualists are polytheists solely because they believe in two necessary existent gods.
Correction: The text clarifies that they are considered polytheists because they affirm multiple objects worthy of worship, not because of the number of necessary existents they affirm.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jurjani, why are dualists considered polytheists?
A) Because they affirm two necessary existent gods.
B) Because they affirm multiple objects worthy of worship.
C) Because they deny the prophethood of Muhammad.
D) Because they reject the oneness of God.

Key Takeaway
Dualists are polytheists due to their worship of multiple beings, not because they assert two necessary existents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's faith based on their theological beliefs rather than their actual objects of worship? How does this lesson challenge you to prioritize the criterion of worship in your understanding of polytheism?
?
This passage equates polytheism with directing worship to multiple beings. In your own life, are there any 'hidden' objects of worship—such as status, wealth, or desires—that you might be prioritizing over Allah? What concrete step will you take to purify your worship this week?
?
If the dualists are condemned for worshipping multiple beings, how does this affect your view of your own daily actions? Are there moments when you seek approval from people or follow your desires as if they were lords? Ask Allah to protect you from hidden shirk and commit to a specific act of worship done solely for Him today.

Beliefs of the Manichaeans
Al-Jurjani describes Manichaean history, beliefs, and a critique of their concept of darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core beliefs and practices of the Manichaean sect as described by al-Jurjani, including their view of light and darkness.

Core Idea
Manichaeans believe in a supreme Light and practice strict rituals, but their view of darkness leads to theological inconsistencies.

This lesson delves into the detailed description of the Manichaeans, one of the major dualist sects. Al-Jurjani covers their founder Mani, their acceptance of earlier prophets, their obligatory prayers, and their problematic conception of darkness as an accident, which implies the pre-eternity of bodies and God's need.

Guided Path
1
Learn about Mani and his timeline
Read the description of Mani, his appearance, and his death. Note the historical context given by al-Jurjani.
Mani was killed after Jesus' mission.
2
Examine Manichaean beliefs
Identify the prophets they believe in and the practices they require, such as four daily prayers and prohibitions.
They believe in many prophets including Adam, Noah, Jesus, and Muhammad.
3
Analyze the problem with their view of darkness
The text points out a logical problem: if darkness is an accident, then bodies must be pre-eternal, and God would need them. This is a criticism of their dualism.
The author suggests they may have meant something else by 'darkness'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا يقولون بإلهين واجبي الوجود إلخ) فعدهم من المشركين لقولهم بتعدد المستحق للعبادة لا لقولهم بواجبي الوجود. قوله: (فالمانوية والديصانية من الثنوية قالوا إلخ) لا فائدة في التخصيص فإن المزدكية أيضاً قالوا بذلك، أما المانوية فهو أصحاب ماني بن ماني الحكيم الذي ظهر في زمان شابور بن از دشير وقتله بهرام بن هرمز بن شابور بعدما بعث عيسى عليه السلام وهم معتقدون في الشرائع والأنبياء وأن أول مبعوث بالحكمة والنبوة آدم عليه السلام ثم شيث ونوح وإبراهيم وزرداشت والمسيح ويونس ومحمد صلوات الله عليه وعلى سائر انبيائه وكانوا يوجبون في اليوم والليلة أربع صلوات ويحرمون الزنا والقتل والسرقة والكذب والسحر وعبادة الأوثان وغير ذلك، وأما الظلمة، وفساده ظاهر لأنهما عرضان فيلزم قدم الجسم وكون الإله محتاجاً إليه وكأنهم أرادوا معنى آخر سوى المتعارف فإنهم قالوا النورحي عالم قادر سميع بصير، والمجوس منهم ذهبوا إلى أن فاعل الخير هو يزدان وفاعل الشر هو اهر من ويعنون به الشيطان، قوله : ( وفاعل الشر هواهر من إلخ) واختلف المجوس في أن أهو من قديم أو حادث من يزدان.
His statement: (They do not affirm two necessary existent gods, etc.) So he counts them among the polytheists because of their claim of multiple objects worthy of worship, not because of their claim of two necessary existents. His statement: (The Manichaeans and the Daysānites among the dualists said, etc.) There is no benefit in specification, for the Mazdakites also said that. As for the Manichaeans, they are the followers of Mani son of Mani the sage, who appeared in the time of Shapur son of Ardashir, and was killed by Bahram son of Hormuz son of Shapur after the mission of Jesus, peace be upon him. They believe in the laws and prophets, and that the first sent with wisdom and prophecy was Adam, peace be upon him, then Seth, Noah, Abraham, Zoroaster, the Messiah, Jonah, and Muhammad, may God's blessings be upon him and all his prophets. They required four prayers each day and night, and forbade adultery, murder, theft, lying, sorcery, idol worship, and other things. As for darkness, its corruption is apparent because they are accidents, necessitating the pre-eternity of the body and the god's need of it. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself thinking of good and evil as almost equal forces in the world? How does the logical flaw in Manichaean dualism challenge that assumption in your own heart?
?
This passage shows that even a seemingly devout group can adopt beliefs that undermine Tawhid. Where in your own religious practice have you unwittingly compromised Allah's oneness by valuing something else too highly?
?
Al-Jurjani points out that accepting many prophets does not prevent theological error. Are there aspects of your faith that you hold simply because others around you hold them, without checking them against the Quran and Sunnah? What would it cost you to examine them today?

Magian Beliefs: Yazdān and Ahriman
Al-Jurjani describes Magian dualism and their internal dispute about the origin of Ahriman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Magian dualist belief in two principles—Yazdān as the creator of good and Ahriman as the creator of evil—and the disagreement over Ahriman's origin.

Core Idea
Magians attribute good to Yazdān and evil to Ahriman, but debate whether Ahriman is pre-eternal or created.

This lesson focuses on the Magians (مجوس), another dualist sect. They distinguish between the creator of good, Yazdān, and the creator of evil, Ahriman (Satan). Al-Jurjani also notes an internal disagreement among them: whether Ahriman is pre-eternal or originated from Yazdān.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two principles
Note how the Magians assign good to Yazdān and evil to Ahriman, whom they identify with Satan.
This is a classic dualist structure.
2
Understand the disagreement
The text states that the Magians differ on whether Ahriman is pre-eternal (qadīm) or originated (ḥadith) from Yazdān. This shows variation within the sect.
This disagreement has theological implications for the nature of evil.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this belief relates to the broader classification of dualists and their polytheism.
The Magians are considered polytheists because they direct worship to both principles, not just one.

Source Text

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the point of disagreement among the Magians?
A) Whether Yazdān is good or evil.
B) Whether Ahriman is pre-eternal or originated from Yazdān.
C) Whether Ahriman is a spirit or a body.
D) Whether they should pray four times a day.

Key Takeaway
The Magians split good and evil between two principles, but disagree on whether the evil principle is eternal or created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Magians split good and evil between two sources, do you see traces of that mindset in your own life — like attributing your successes to yourself and your failures to others or to circumstances? How can you train yourself to see both as coming from Allah alone?
?
The Magians disagreed on whether Ahriman is eternal or created. Have you ever settled into a comfortable belief about the origin of evil without examining it? Will you commit today to seeking a deeper understanding of why Allah allows evil, not just accepting a pat answer?
?
Consider a time you disagreed with fellow Muslims on a matter of faith. Did you handle that disagreement with the same grace the Magians failed to show? What one step will you take to ensure that your differences do not lead to division but to deeper unity in tawheed?

Manichaeans and Mazdakites: Light and Darkness
Description of Manichaean and Mazdakite dualism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key differences between the Manichaean and Mazdakite dualist systems regarding the nature and actions of light and darkness.

Core Idea
Dualists agree on two origins but split on whether light acts with intention or nature.

The commentator begins by describing the followers of Diṣān, known as the Manichaeans, and notes their similarity to the Mazdakites. Both believe in the pre-eternity of light and darkness, but they differ crucially on the attributes of these principles. This lesson explores that distinction and sets the stage for understanding the variety within dualist thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Manichaeans and Mazdakites
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the names and the core beliefs attributed to each group.
Pay attention to the contrast between 'intention and choice' for light versus 'accident and nature' for darkness.
2
Identify the differences
Compare how each sect describes light (knowing, sensing, volitional) and darkness (ignorant, blind, accidental vs. natural).
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why these differences matter for understanding dualist theology and the problem of evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن بعض الديصانية فهم أصحاب ديصان ومعتقدهم معتقد المزدكية أصحاب مزدك الذي ظهر في زمن نوشروان وهو قدم النور والظلمة على الوجه الذي اعتقده المانوية إلا أن المزدكية يقولون النور عالم حساس وأنه يفعل ما يفعل بالقصد والاختيار بخلاف الظلام فإنه جاهل أعمى وإن ما يفعله بحكم الاتفاق والخبط والديصانية يخالفونهم في ذلك، ويقولون ما يحدث من الشركان عن الظلام بطبعه لا بحكم الاتفاق، وللثنوية فرقتان آخريان يقال لهم المرقونية والكمونية، أما المرقونية فقد وافقوا من تقدم ذكره في إثبات النور والظلمة وخالفوه في إثبات أصل ثالث هو المعدل الجامع بين النور والظلمة قالوا وذلك الأصل دون النور في المرتبة وفوق الظلمة، وأما الكمونية فقالوا أصول العالم ثلاثة النار والماء والأرض فالنار خير بطبعها يصدر منها الخيرات المحضة، والماء ضدها يصدر منه الشرور المحضة، ومالحان متوسطاً فمن الأرض، وهؤلاء هم المتعقدون في النار وعن مذهبم نشأ اتخاذ بيوت النيران في البلدان وعبادتها تعظيما لها. قوله: (وكأنهم أرادوا إلخ) قال في الإبكار معتقداً لمانوية أن النور والظلمة جسمان قديمان أبديان حساسان سميعان بصيران. قوله ( والمجوس منهم) سياق كلام الشارح صريح في أن المجوس من الثنوية وسياق كلام الآمدي صريح في خلافه، حيث قال أولاً الفرع السادس خلافه، حيث قال أولا الفرع السادس في الرد على الثنوية والمجوس، أما الثنوية فخمس وفصل فرقها ثم قال: وأما المجوس فقد اتفقوا أيضاً على أن أصل العالم النور والظلمة كمذهب الثنوية وقد اختلفوا وتفرقوا فرقاً أربعاً، ثم فصل فرقها وما ذكره الشارح أظهر. قوله : ( وفاعل الشر هواهر من (إلخ) واختلف المجوس في أن أهو من قديم أو حادث من يزدان.
From some of the Diṣāniyyah: they are the followers of Diṣān, and their creed is the creed of the Mazdakites, the followers of Mazdak who appeared in the time of Nushirwan, which is the eternity of light and darkness in the manner that the Manichaeans believed, except that the Mazdakites say that light is knowing, sensing, and that it acts with intention and choice, unlike darkness which is ignorant and blind, and that what it does is by accident and confusion. The Diṣāniyyah differ from them in that, and they say that what occurs of evil from darkness is by its nature, not by accident. And there are two other sects of dualists called the Marcionites and the Chemonites. As for the Marcionites, they agreed with those mentioned earlier in affirming light and darkness, but disagreed with them in affirming a third principle which is the equalizer combining light and darkness; they said that this principle is below light in rank and above darkness. As for the Chemonites, they said the principles of the world are three: fire, water, and earth. Fire is good by nature, from it come pure good things; water is its opposite, from it come pure evil things; and a middle thing from earth. These are the believers in fire, and from their doctrine arose the establishment of fire temples in the lands and worshipping them as a veneration. His saying: (As if they meant, etc.) He said in al-Ibkār: the Manichaean belief is that light and darkness are two bodies, eternal, everlasting, sensing, hearing, seeing. His saying: (And the Magians are among them) The context of the commentator's speech is explicit that the Magians are among the dualists, and the context of Āmidī's speech is explicit in the opposite, where he first said: the sixth branch: in refutation of the dualists and the Magians. As for the dualists, they are five, and he detailed their sects, then said: As for the Magians, they also agreed that the origin of the world is light and darkness like the doctrine of the dualists, and they differed and split into four sects, then he detailed their sects. What the commentator mentioned is more apparent. His saying: (And the doer of evil is Ahriman, etc.) The Magians differed concerning whether Ahriman is eternal or originated from Yazdān.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a doxographical survey of dualist sects. It begins by discussing the followers of Diṣān (Manichaeans) and notes that their creed resembles that of the Mazdakites, who believe in the pre-eternity of light and darkness but differ on the nature of light (volitional and knowledgeable) and darkness (accidental vs. natural). Then it introduces two more sects: the Marcionites, who add a third mediating principle between light and darkness, and the Chemonites, who posit three elements (fire, water, earth) with fire as purely good, water as purely evil, and earth as a mixture, leading to fire worship. The passage then comments on the Magians: the commentator considers them dualists, but al-Āmidī apparently does not. The Magians also believe in light and darkness as origins but split into four sects themselves. Finally, it notes their internal disagreement over whether Ahriman (the evil principle) is eternal or originated from Yazdān.

Key Terms
ديصانية
مزدكية
نور
ظلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume all dualists believe both light and darkness are equally active and aware.
Correction: The Mazdakites and Manichaeans differ: Mazdakites see light as intentional and darkness as accidental, while Manichaeans see darkness as naturally evil.

Checkpoint
What do the Mazdakites claim about light?
A) Light acts by nature
B) Light acts by intention and choice
C) Light is ignorant and blind
D) Light is eternal but inactive

Key Takeaway
The Mazdakites and Manichaeans both believe in light and darkness as eternal principles, but they disagree on whether darkness acts accidentally or naturally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or evil in your life, do you ever feel like it comes from a blind, indifferent force? How does the Islamic teaching that everything happens by Allah's decree and wisdom challenge you to change that perception? What one thought pattern will you actively correct today?
?
The Mazdakites believed light acts with intention and choice. Do you live as though you are a passive victim of circumstances (like darkness acting by accident), or do you take intentional, chosen action as a believer? Which of your daily habits reflects that you are a creature of purpose? Make a specific intention to change one habit this week.
?
If you truly believe that all good comes from Allah and all evil is permitted by Him for a wise purpose, does your heart accept that or does it secretly resent Allah when things go wrong? Spend time in sujood today asking Allah to grant you contentment with His decree.

Marcionites and Chemonites: Adding Principles
Enumeration of two additional dualist sects with distinct principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Marcionites and Chemonites diverge from standard dualism by introducing a third principle or element system.

Core Idea
Dualism is not always two principles; some sects add a mediating element.

After discussing the Manichaeans and Mazdakites, the commentator turns to two more dualist sects: the Marcionites and the Chemonites. These groups modify the classic two-principle system. The Marcionites introduce a third, reconciling entity, while the Chemonites replace the duality with three elements. This lesson clarifies these variations.

Guided Path
1
Read about the Marcionites
Read the first part that describes the Marcionite belief in a third principle that is an equalizer between light and darkness.
2
Read about the Chemonites
Read the second part that describes the Chemonite system of three elements: fire, water, and earth.
3
Compare with standard dualism
Notice how these sects move beyond a simple two-principle model and consider the implications for fire worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن بعض الديصانية فهم أصحاب ديصان ومعتقدهم معتقد المزدكية أصحاب مزدك الذي ظهر في زمن نوشروان وهو قدم النور والظلمة على الوجه الذي اعتقده المانوية إلا أن المزدكية يقولون النور عالم حساس وأنه يفعل ما يفعل بالقصد والاختيار بخلاف الظلام فإنه جاهل أعمى وإن ما يفعله بحكم الاتفاق والخبط والديصانية يخالفونهم في ذلك، ويقولون ما يحدث من الشركان عن الظلام بطبعه لا بحكم الاتفاق، وللثنوية فرقتان آخريان يقال لهم المرقونية والكمونية، أما المرقونية فقد وافقوا من تقدم ذكره في إثبات النور والظلمة وخالفوه في إثبات أصل ثالث هو المعدل الجامع بين النور والظلمة قالوا وذلك الأصل دون النور في المرتبة وفوق الظلمة، وأما الكمونية فقالوا أصول العالم ثلاثة النار والماء والأرض فالنار خير بطبعها يصدر منها الخيرات المحضة، والماء ضدها يصدر منه الشرور المحضة، ومالحان متوسطاً فمن الأرض، وهؤلاء هم المتعقدون في النار وعن مذهبم نشأ اتخاذ بيوت النيران في البلدان وعبادتها تعظيما لها. قوله: (وكأنهم أرادوا إلخ) قال في الإبكار معتقداً لمانوية أن النور والظلمة جسمان قديمان أبديان حساسان سميعان بصيران. قوله ( والمجوس منهم) سياق كلام الشارح صريح في أن المجوس من الثنوية وسياق كلام الآمدي صريح في خلافه، حيث قال أولاً الفرع السادس خلافه، حيث قال أولا الفرع السادس في الرد على الثنوية والمجوس، أما الثنوية فخمس وفصل فرقها ثم قال: وأما المجوس فقد اتفقوا أيضاً على أن أصل العالم النور والظلمة كمذهب الثنوية وقد اختلفوا وتفرقوا فرقاً أربعاً، ثم فصل فرقها وما ذكره الشارح أظهر. قوله : ( وفاعل الشر هواهر من (إلخ) واختلف المجوس في أن أهو من قديم أو حادث من يزدان.
From some of the Diṣāniyyah: they are the followers of Diṣān, and their creed is the creed of the Mazdakites, the followers of Mazdak who appeared in the time of Nushirwan, which is the eternity of light and darkness in the manner that the Manichaeans believed, except that the Mazdakites say that light is knowing, sensing, and that it acts with intention and choice, unlike darkness which is ignorant and blind, and that what it does is by accident and confusion. The Diṣāniyyah differ from them in that, and they say that what occurs of evil from darkness is by its nature, not by accident. And there are two other sects of dualists called the Marcionites and the Chemonites. As for the Marcionites, they agreed with those mentioned earlier in affirming light and darkness, but disagreed with them in affirming a third principle which is the equalizer combining light and darkness; they said that this principle is below light in rank and above darkness. As for the Chemonites, they said the principles of the world are three: fire, water, and earth. Fire is good by nature, from it come pure good things; water is its opposite, from it come pure evil things; and a middle thing from earth. These are the believers in fire, and from their doctrine arose the establishment of fire temples in the lands and worshipping them as a veneration. His saying: (As if they meant, etc.) He said in al-Ibkār: the Manichaean belief is that light and darkness are two bodies, eternal, everlasting, sensing, hearing, seeing. His saying: (And the Magians are among them) The context of the commentator's speech is explicit that the Magians are among the dualists, and the context of Āmidī's speech is explicit in the opposite, where he first said: the sixth branch: in refutation of the dualists and the Magians. As for the dualists, they are five, and he detailed their sects, then said: As for the Magians, they also agreed that the origin of the world is light and darkness like the doctrine of the dualists, and they differed and split into four sects, then he detailed their sects. What the commentator mentioned is more apparent. His saying: (And the doer of evil is Ahriman, etc.) The Magians differed concerning whether Ahriman is eternal or originated from Yazdān.

Commentary
This passage is a doxographical survey of dualist sects. It begins by discussing the followers of Diṣān (Manichaeans) and notes that their creed resembles that of the Mazdakites, who believe in the pre-eternity of light and darkness but differ on the nature of light (volitional and knowledgeable) and darkness (accidental vs. natural). How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt the need to add your own principles to reconcile God's justice with His mercy, rather than accepting His revelation as sufficient? How does the Marcionites' invented mediator warn you against inserting human reasoning into divine attributes?
?
When you see people venerating creation—like fire in this lesson—what idols have you unknowingly set up in your heart that compete with your devotion to the Creator alone?
?
The Chemonites regarded fire as purely good and water as purely evil. Do you ever divide the world into absolute good and absolute evil based on your own preferences, forgetting that only Allah is the source of all good and that He alone defines evil? Will you commit to using the Quran and Sunnah as your measure instead of your feelings?

Magians: Dualists or Not?
Classification of Magians and their internal divisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether the Magians should be classified as dualists and their internal divisions.

Core Idea
Whether Magians are dualists is disputed among scholars.

The final part of the passage deals with the Magians, who are often associated with dualism due to their belief in a good and evil principle. However, the commentator notes a disagreement with al-Āmidī about their classification. This lesson explores that debate and the Magians' own internal splits.

Guided Path
1
Read the commentator's statement
Read the sentence where the commentator says the Magians are among the dualists, and note al-Āmidī's opposing view.
2
Understand the Magians' beliefs
Read the description that Magians also affirm light and darkness as origins and their division into four sects.
3
Reflect on the disagreement
Consider why scholars might differ on whether Magians are dualists, given their additional beliefs.

Mu'tazila and Shi'a Argument on Attributes
Presents the first argument of the Mu'tazila and Shi'a against additional attributes and the answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument of the Mu'tazila and Shi'a against additional divine attributes and the response that distinguishes between multiple eternal beings and a single essence.

Core Idea
Affirming multiple attributes is not the same as affirming multiple gods.

This passage introduces the first of three arguments from the Mu'tazila and Shi'a against the view that God's attributes are real and distinct from His essence. They claim that positing multiple eternal entities is akin to Christian tritheism and thus unbelief. The answer provides a crucial distinction: unbelief lies in affirming multiple independent eternal beings, not in affirming one essence with attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage aloud and then the English translation. Notice the concise style: it states the argument and then the answer.
The passage uses the phrase 'ما مر' referring to previously mentioned content.
2
Identify the two components
Identify the argument (that establishing multiple eternals is kufr like the Christians) and the answer (that kufr is establishing multiple eternal beings, not one essence).
The argument uses analogy with Christianity; the answer refines the definition of kufr.
3
Understand the distinction
Reflect on the difference between 'multiple eternal beings' (ذوات قديمة) and 'one essence' (ذات واحدة). The answer denies that attributes are separate beings.
This distinction is crucial to defending the doctrine of attributes without falling into polytheism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجت المعتزلة والشيعة بوجوه ثلاثة: الأول ما مر من أن إثبات القدماء كفر بهم كفرت النصاری. والجواب ما مر أيضاً من أن الكفر إثبات ذوات قديمة لا إثبات ذات واحدة.
And the Mu'tazila and Shi'a argued with three arguments. The first is what has already been mentioned: that establishing multiple eternals is unbelief, as the Christians were disbelieved for it. The answer is also what has already been mentioned: that unbelief is establishing multiple eternal beings, not establishing one essence.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents the first of three arguments from the Mu'tazila and Shi'a against the view that God has real, additional attributes. Their argument is that affirming multiple eternal entities (the attributes) would be similar to the Christian belief in multiple eternal persons of the Trinity, which is considered unbelief. The answer provided is a distinction: unbelief consists in affirming multiple independent eternal beings, not in affirming a single essence with attributes that are not separate entities. This answer suggests that the attributes are not independent existents, thus avoiding the charge of polytheism.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الشيعة
القدماء
الكفر
ذوات قديمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming multiple attributes of God implies multiple gods, similar to the Christian Trinity.
Correction: The answer clarifies that unbelief is affirming multiple independent eternal beings (ذوات قديمة), not affirming a single essence (ذات واحدة) with attributes that are not separate entities.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument of the Mu'tazila and Shi'a against additional attributes?
A) Attributes are impossible.
B) Affirming multiple eternals is unbelief like the Christians.
C) Attributes are created.
D) Attributes are irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Shi'a argue that affirming multiple eternal attributes is like Christian polytheism, but the answer clarifies that unbelief is affirming multiple independent eternal beings, not a single essence with attributes.

?

?
